## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, nonlinear stiffness, damping, and potential driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Full Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric + cubic nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping with sign)
- Coulomb + viscous: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v**3 (general nonlinear terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry about equilibrium — expect these in symmetric potential wells
- Even-power position terms (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials or broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent linear energy dissipation or gain (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of position powers and velocity (e.g., x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping, characteristic of van der Pol-type self-excited oscillators
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic forcing/driving
- Negative coefficient on the linear x term (restoring) combined with positive coefficient on x**3 suggests a double-well (Duffing) potential
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative or dissipative) govern dynamics
- Odd-power velocity terms (v**3) represent nonlinear drag forces that grow superlinearly with speed

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.752289977167006*v*(1 - x**2) - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Let me expand this:
`0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.752289977167006*v - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Combining v terms:
`-1.366031954203476*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

So the GT has the form:
- `A*x**3` (coefficient on x³)
- `B*v` (constant times v)
- `C*v*x**2` (v times x²)
- `D*v*exp(-|x|)` (v times exp(-|x|))

The key challenge is the `exp(-|x|)` term. Most candidates have `exp(c*x)`, not `exp(-|x|)`.

For `exp(-|x|)`: when x > 0, this is `exp(-x)`, and when x < 0, this is `exp(x)`. The function `exp(c*x)` with a single constant c cannot replicate `exp(-|x|)` because it would need to be `exp(-x)` for positive x and `exp(x)` for negative x simultaneously. No single value of c works for all x.

So I need to check: can any candidate reproduce `exp(-|x|)` behavior?

Looking through the candidates, most use `exp(c*x)` which cannot match `exp(-|x|)`. Let me check for special cases:

- Candidate 1: `c2*v*exp(c3*x) + c4*v*log(c5*x**2 + 1)` - exp(c3*x) can't match exp(-|x|), and log(c5*x²+1) can't compensate.

- Candidate 25: Has `v*log(c7*x**2 + 1)` - log is not exp(-|x|).

- Candidate 31: Has both `v*log(c4*x**2+1)` and `v*exp(c6*x)` - neither matches exp(-|x|).

None of the candidates contain `exp(-Abs(x))` or any equivalent construction. The function `exp(-|x|)` is non-analytic at x=0 and cannot be represented by any finite combination of smooth functions like `exp(cx)`, polynomials, `sin`, `cos`, `log`, etc.

However, let me reconsider. Could candidates with multiple exponential-like terms approximate or exactly match? For exact equivalence, `exp(-|x|)` cannot be written as a finite sum of `x^n * exp(c*x)` terms because those are smooth everywhere while `exp(-|x|)` has a kink at x=0.

Wait - Candidate 40 has `v*x**c6*exp(c7*x)`. If c6=0, this gives `v*exp(c7*x)`, still smooth.

Candidate 43 has `v*x**c6*exp(c7*x)` - same issue.

None of the candidates can produce `exp(-|x|)` which is the key non-smooth term in the GT.

But wait - looking again at the GT symbolic expression: `-beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v`. The `Abs(x)` makes this non-analytic. No candidate formula contains `Abs(x)` in an exponential (some have `Abs(v)` but not `Abs(x)`).

Since `exp(-|x|)` cannot be exactly represented by any combination of smooth functions of x (polynomials, exp(cx), sin, cos, log, etc.), and none of the candidates contain `Abs(x)`, no candidate can exactly match the GT for all values of x.

Therefore, none of the candidates can be made equivalent to the GT.
